<p><b>Kazan</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span>-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span><span title="/ɑː/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">ɑː</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Tatar_language" title="Tatar language">Tatar</a>&#58; <span lang="tt" title="Tatar-language text">Казан</span>; Russian&#58; <span lang="ru" title="Russian-language text">Каза́нь</span>, <small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian" title="Help:IPA/Russian">[kɐˈzanʲ]</a></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> and largest city of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Tatarstan" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Tatarstan">Republic of Tatarstan</a> in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>. The city lies at the <a href="/wiki/Confluence" title="Confluence">confluence</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Volga" title="Volga">Volga</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kazanka_(river)" title="Kazanka (river)">Kazanka</a> rivers, covering an area of 425.3 square kilometres (164.2 square miles), with a population of over 1.2 million residents,<sup id="cite_ref-est.2020_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-est.2020-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> up to roughly 1.6 million residents in the urban agglomeration. Kazan is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Russia_by_population" title="List of cities and towns in Russia by population">fifth-largest city</a> in Russia, and the <a href="/wiki/Volga#Biggest_cities_on_the_shores_of_the_Volga" title="Volga">most populous city</a> on the Volga, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Volga_Federal_District" title="Volga Federal District">Volga Federal District</a>.
</p><p>Ancient Kazan was founded in the late 13th century by the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a>. In 1438, Kazan became the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Kazan" title="Khanate of Kazan">Khanate of Kazan</a>. In 1552, Kazan was captured by <a href="/wiki/Ivan_the_Terrible" title="Ivan the Terrible">Ivan the Terrible</a> and became a part of Russia. The city was seized and largely destroyed during <a href="/wiki/Pugachev%27s_Rebellion" title="Pugachev&#39;s Rebellion">Pugachev's Rebellion</a> of 1773–75, but was later rebuilt during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine the Great</a>. In the following centuries, Kazan grew to become a major industrial, cultural and religious centre of Russia. In 1920, after the <a href="/wiki/Russian_SFSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian SFSR">Russian SFSR</a> became a part of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, Kazan became the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Tatar_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Tatar Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Tatar ASSR</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>, Kazan stayed as the capital of the Republic of Tatarstan.
</p><p>Kazan is renowned for its vibrant mix of Tatar and Russian cultures.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, 2.1 million tourists visited Kazan, and 1.5 million tourists visited the <a href="/wiki/Kazan_Kremlin" title="Kazan Kremlin">Kazan Kremlin</a>, a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In April 2009, the Russian Patent Office granted Kazan the right to brand itself as the "Third Capital of Russia".<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>  In 2009 it was chosen as the "Sports capital of Russia",<sup id="cite_ref-sportcap_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sportcap-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and it still is referred to as such.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Kazan hosted the <a href="/wiki/2013_Summer_Universiade" title="2013 Summer Universiade">2013 Summer Universiade</a>, and was one of the host cities of the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The term kazan means 'boiler' or 'cauldron' (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: Каза́н/<a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatar</a>:казан) in the <a href="/wiki/Tatar_language" title="Tatar language">Tatar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic</a> languages. The origin of the city and its name is often described as follows: a sorcerer advised the Bulgars to build a city where, without any fire, a boiler dug into the ground would boil water. As a result, a similar place was founded on the shore of <a href="/wiki/Kaban_Lakes" title="Kaban Lakes">Lake Kaban</a>. One legend claims that the city was named after the river <a href="/wiki/Kazanka_(river)" title="Kazanka (river)">Kazanka</a>, which was named after the son of a Bulgar governor who dropped a copper cauldron into it.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Kazan" title="History of Kazan">History of Kazan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Kazan" title="Timeline of Kazan">Timeline of Kazan</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">February 2020</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CasanTartarorum_by_Olearius.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/CasanTartarorum_by_Olearius.jpg/220px-CasanTartarorum_by_Olearius.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/CasanTartarorum_by_Olearius.jpg/330px-CasanTartarorum_by_Olearius.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/CasanTartarorum_by_Olearius.jpg/440px-CasanTartarorum_by_Olearius.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="743" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CasanTartarorum_by_Olearius.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of Kazan by <a href="/wiki/Adam_Olearius" title="Adam Olearius">Adam Olearius</a>, 1630</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8_%D0%B2_1767_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%83.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8_%D0%B2_1767_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%83.jpg/220px-%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8_%D0%B2_1767_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%83.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="80" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8_%D0%B2_1767_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%83.jpg/330px-%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8_%D0%B2_1767_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%83.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8_%D0%B2_1767_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%83.jpg/440px-%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8_%D0%B2_1767_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%83.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1147" data-file-height="415" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8_%D0%B2_1767_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%83.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of the city c. 1767</div></div></div>
<p>According to the official version adopted today, the city was founded more than 1,000 years ago. The estimated date of the urban settlement on the site of Kazan is 1004–1005 AD. The reason for this dating was found during excavations in the Kazan Kremlin - a Czech coin, dated by the Board of <a href="/wiki/Wenceslaus_I,_Duke_of_Bohemia" title="Wenceslaus I, Duke of Bohemia">St. Wenceslaus</a> (presumably, coinage 929–930 years) and the earliest Czech coin, the remains of masonry and wooden city fence, handicrafts and utensils (Hungarian type lining, women's beads, etc.), as well as other artifacts with less obvious dating. According to official statements, experts from 20 cities of Russia and 22 countries of the world were involved in the study of findings related to the age of Kazan.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kazan was a border post between <a href="/wiki/Volga_Bulgaria" title="Volga Bulgaria">Volga Bulgaria</a> and two <a href="/wiki/Finno-Ugric_peoples" title="Finno-Ugric peoples">Finno-Ugric peoples</a>—the <a href="/wiki/Mari_people" title="Mari people">Mari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Udmurt_people" title="Udmurt people">Udmurt</a>. Another vexatious question is where the citadel was built originally. Archaeological explorations have produced evidence of urban settlement in three parts of the modern city: in the <a href="/wiki/Kazan_Kremlin" title="Kazan Kremlin">Kremlin</a>; in Bişbalta at the site of the modern Zilantaw monastery; and near the <a href="/wiki/Qaban_lake" class="mw-redirect" title="Qaban lake">Qaban lake</a>. The oldest of these seems to be the Kremlin.
</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Volga_Bulgaria" title="Mongol invasion of Volga Bulgaria">Mongols ravaged the Bolğar and Bilär territories</a> in the 13th century, the surviving Bulgars recovered in numbers and a small number of <a href="/wiki/Kipchaks" title="Kipchaks">Kipchaks</a> were assimilated from which they adopted their language (the so-called Bulgarism), or Kipchaks and Bulgars mixed to create a modern Kazan-Tatar population. Some Tatars also went to Lithuania, brought by Vytautas the great. Kazan became the center of the Principality, which was dependent on The Golden Horde. In the 13th and 14th centuries, Kazan was growing, becoming an important trade and political center within The <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a>. The growth of the city was also promoted by the successful geographical location at the intersection of major trade routes connecting East and West. During the same period, the minting of currency began with the indication of the place of minting—"Bulgar al-Jadid", that is, a New Bulgar.
</p><p>In 1438, the Bulgar fortress Kazan (ISKE-Kazan) was captured by the ousted Golden Horde Khan <a href="/wiki/Ulugh_Muhammad" title="Ulugh Muhammad">Ulugh Muhammad</a>, who killed the local Prince Swan and moved the fortress to a modern place (according to Russian Chronicles). The city became the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Kazan_Khanate" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazan Khanate">Kazan Khanate</a>. The city Bazaar, Taş Ayaq (stone foot) has become the most important shopping center in the region, especially for furniture. Handicraft production also flourished, as the city gained a reputation for its leather and gold products, as well as the wealth of its palaces and mosques. 
Kazan had trade relations with Moscow, Crimea, Turkey and other regions.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_Tsardom_period">Russian Tsardom period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Russian Tsardom period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%84%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80._%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C.1894.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%84%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80._%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C.1894.jpg/220px-%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%84%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80._%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C.1894.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%84%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80._%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C.1894.jpg/330px-%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%84%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80._%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C.1894.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%84%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80._%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C.1894.jpg/440px-%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%84%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80._%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C.1894.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="509" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%84%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80._%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C.1894.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Annunciation Cathedral of Kazan Kremlin, 1561–1562</div></div></div>
<p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Kazan" title="Siege of Kazan">Siege of Kazan</a> in 1552, <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia" title="Tsardom of Russia">Tsar</a> <a href="/wiki/Ivan_the_Terrible" title="Ivan the Terrible">Ivan the Terrible</a> conquered the city and massacred the majority of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-translate.google.ru_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-translate.google.ru-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> During the subsequent governorship of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Gorbatyi-Shuisky" title="Alexander Gorbatyi-Shuisky">Alexander Gorbatyi-Shuisky</a>, most of the Kazan's Tatar residents were forcibly Christianized or deported,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Kerashen_Tatars" class="mw-redirect" title="Kerashen Tatars">Kerashen Tatars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-translate.google.ru_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-translate.google.ru-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">Mosques</a> and palaces were ruined.<sup id="cite_ref-translate.google.ru_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-translate.google.ru-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The surviving Tatar population was moved to a place 50 kilometers (31&#160;mi) away from the city and this place was forcibly settled by Russian farmers and soldiers. <a href="/wiki/Serving_Tatars" title="Serving Tatars">Tatars in the Russian service</a> were settled in the Tatar Bistäse settlement near the city's wall. Later Tatar merchants and handicraft masters also settled there. During this period, Kazan was largely destroyed as a result of several great fires. After one of them in 1579, the icon <i><a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Kazan" title="Our Lady of Kazan">Our Lady of Kazan</a></i> was discovered in the city.
</p><p>In the early 17th century, at the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Time_of_Troubles" title="Time of Troubles">Time of Troubles</a> in Russia, the Tsardom of Kazan declared independence under the leadership of voyvoda Nikanor Shulgin with the help of the Russian population, but this independence was suppressed by <a href="/wiki/Kuzma_Minin" title="Kuzma Minin">Kuzma Minin</a> in 1612.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_Empire_period">Russian Empire period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Russian Empire period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazanmap19century.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Kazanmap19century.jpg/220px-Kazanmap19century.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Kazanmap19century.jpg/330px-Kazanmap19century.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Kazanmap19century.jpg/440px-Kazanmap19century.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5080" data-file-height="3214" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazanmap19century.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kazan city map from the 19th century, Russian edition</div></div></div>
<p>In 1708, the Tsardom of Kazan was abolished, and Kazan became the seat of <a href="/wiki/Kazan_Governorate" title="Kazan Governorate">Kazan Governorate</a>. After <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">Peter the Great</a>'s visit, the city became a center of shipbuilding for the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_fleet" class="mw-redirect" title="Caspian fleet">Caspian fleet</a>. The major Russian poet <a href="/wiki/Gavrila_Derzhavin" title="Gavrila Derzhavin">Gavrila Derzhavin</a> was born in Kazan in 1743, the son of a poor country squire of Tatar ancestry though himself having a thoroughly Russian identity.
</p><p>Before the building of modern dams, low-lying areas were regularly flooded in April and May. Kazan suffered major fires in 1595, 1672, 1694, 1742, 1749, 1757, 1774, 1815, and 1842.
</p><p>Kazan was <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kazan_(1774)" title="Battle of Kazan (1774)">largely destroyed in</a> 1774 as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Pugachev%27s_Rebellion" title="Pugachev&#39;s Rebellion">Pugachev revolt (1774–1776)</a>, an uprising by border troops and peasants led by the <a href="/wiki/Don_Cossack" class="mw-redirect" title="Don Cossack">Don Cossack</a> <a href="/wiki/Ataman" title="Ataman">ataman</a> (Captain) <a href="/wiki/Yemelyan_Pugachev" title="Yemelyan Pugachev">Yemelyan Pugachev</a>, but the city, formerly largely of timber construction, was soon afterwards rebuilt, using stone and according to a grid pattern plan, during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine the Great</a>. Catherine also decreed that mosques could again be built in Kazan, the first being <a href="/wiki/Marjani_Mosque" class="mw-redirect" title="Marjani Mosque">Marjani Mosque</a>.
</p><p>At the beginning of the 19th century <a href="/wiki/Kazan_State_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazan State University">Kazan State University</a> and printing press were founded by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia" title="Alexander I of Russia">Alexander I</a>. It became an important center for <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Studies" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriental Studies">Oriental Studies</a> in Russia. The <a href="/wiki/Qur%27an" class="mw-redirect" title="Qur&#39;an">Qur'an</a> was first printed in Kazan in 1801. Kazan became an industrial center and peasants migrated there to join its industrial workforce. In 1875, a <a href="/wiki/Horse_tramway" class="mw-redirect" title="Horse tramway">horse tramway</a> appeared; 1899 saw the installation of a <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">tramway</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution_of_1905" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Revolution of 1905">Russian Revolution of 1905</a>, Tatars were allowed to revive Kazan as a Tatar cultural center. The first Tatar theater and the first Tatar newspaper appeared.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_period">Soviet period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Soviet period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1917, Kazan became one of the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">revolution</a> centers. In 1918, Kazan was the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Idel-Ural_State" title="Idel-Ural State">Idel-Ural State</a>, which was suppressed by the <a href="/wiki/Bolshevist" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevist">Bolshevist</a> government. In the <a href="/wiki/Kazan_Operation" title="Kazan Operation">Kazan Operation</a> of August 1918, it was briefly occupied by <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovak_Legions" class="mw-redirect" title="Czechoslovak Legions">Czechoslovak Legions</a>. In 1920, Kazan became the center of <a href="/wiki/Tatar_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Tatar Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Tatar Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic</a>. 
After the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rapallo_(1922)" title="Treaty of Rapallo (1922)">Treaty of Rapallo (1922)</a> until 1933, the German and the Russian army operated together the <a href="/wiki/Kama_tank_school" title="Kama tank school">Kama tank school</a> in Kazan.
</p><p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, many industrial plants and factories to the west were relocated in Kazan, making the city a center of the <a href="/wiki/Military_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Military industry">military industry</a>, producing <a href="/wiki/Tank" title="Tank">tanks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airplane" title="Airplane">planes</a>. After the war Kazan consolidated as an industrial and scientific center. In 1979, the city's population reached one million.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_period">Modern period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Modern period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_172139_Dmitry_Medvedev_visits_Kazan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/RIAN_archive_172139_Dmitry_Medvedev_visits_Kazan.jpg/220px-RIAN_archive_172139_Dmitry_Medvedev_visits_Kazan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/RIAN_archive_172139_Dmitry_Medvedev_visits_Kazan.jpg/330px-RIAN_archive_172139_Dmitry_Medvedev_visits_Kazan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/RIAN_archive_172139_Dmitry_Medvedev_visits_Kazan.jpg/440px-RIAN_archive_172139_Dmitry_Medvedev_visits_Kazan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="622" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_172139_Dmitry_Medvedev_visits_Kazan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a> visits Kazan.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazan,_Baumana_street_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Kazan%2C_Baumana_street_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Kazan%2C_Baumana_street_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Kazan%2C_Baumana_street_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Kazan%2C_Baumana_street_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Kazan%2C_Baumana_street_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Kazan%2C_Baumana_street_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3098" data-file-height="2074" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazan,_Baumana_street_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bauman_Street,_Kazan" title="Bauman Street, Kazan">Bauman street</a></div></div></div>
<p>In the late 1980s and in the 1990s, after the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>, Kazan again became the center of <a href="/wiki/Tatar" class="mw-redirect" title="Tatar">Tatar</a> culture and identity, and separatist tendencies intensified. With the return of capitalism, Kazan became one of the most important centers of the Russian Federation. The city went from 10th to 8th position in population ranking of Russian cities. In the early 2000s, the city earned the right to host both the <a href="/wiki/2013_Summer_Universiade" title="2013 Summer Universiade">2013 Summer Universiade</a> and <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Millennium_of_Kazan">Millennium of Kazan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Millennium of Kazan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Millennium_Bridge_Kazan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Millennium_Bridge_Kazan.jpg/220px-Millennium_Bridge_Kazan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Millennium_Bridge_Kazan.jpg/330px-Millennium_Bridge_Kazan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Millennium_Bridge_Kazan.jpg/440px-Millennium_Bridge_Kazan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="721" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Millennium_Bridge_Kazan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Millennium Bridge</div></div></div>
<p>Since 2000, the city has been undergoing a total renovation. The historical center—including the Kremlin—has been rebuilt, however a large number of the city's historical districts were completely demolished in the renovation. Kazan celebrated its millennium in 2005, after a city-organized historical commission settled on 1005 as the official year of the city's founding.<sup id="cite_ref-Foundation_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Foundation-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> During the millennium celebrations, one of the largest mosque in Russia, <a href="/wiki/Qolsharif_mosque" class="mw-redirect" title="Qolsharif mosque">Qolsharif</a>, was dedicated in the Kazan Kremlin, the holiest copy of <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Kazan" title="Our Lady of Kazan">Our Lady of Kazan</a> was returned to the city, the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Bridge_(Kazan)" title="Millennium Bridge (Kazan)">Millennium Bridge</a> was inaugurated that year,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Kazan_Metro" title="Kazan Metro">Kazan Metro</a> began operation. The government of the Russian Federation released the <a href="/wiki/Medal_%22In_Commemoration_of_the_1000th_Anniversary_of_Kazan%22" title="Medal &quot;In Commemoration of the 1000th Anniversary of Kazan&quot;">Medal "In Commemoration of the 1000th Anniversary of Kazan"</a>.
In 2010, for the preparations to the 2013 Universiade, Kazan began even more renovation by modernizing its airport, fixing the streets, enhancing public transport, and adopting Russian, English, and Tatar languages in all transportation, large stores, and shopping centers.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Heraldry">Heraldry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Heraldry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The historical symbol of Kazan is the mythical dragon-like creature <a href="/wiki/Zilant" title="Zilant">Zilant</a>, often mentioned in legends. For example, when numerous snakes and reptiles severely hampered the development of the city, the hunters went in search of the King of snakes and defeated him, according to another version, the residents of the city bought off the giant snake with gold, after which all the snakes left the city. Another legend says that the giant dragon-like serpent always guarded the Khan's treasures, and that it still protects the hidden wealth before the capture of the city in the secret caves. Historically, it is true that snakes were once numerous in the Kazan region, but then their number has decreased dramatically. The first official coat of arms of Kazan was approved on 18 October 1781 and was described as "black snake under the crown of gold, Kazan, red wings, white field". In 1926, the country introduced a ban on such heraldry. In the 1980s, the coat of arms of Kazan began to reappear, and in the 1990s Kazan Zilant in various styles began to appear in print media. Modern graphics of the emblem and flag appeared in 2005—in a silver field on the green earth a black dragon with red wings and tongue, with gold paws, claws and eyes, topped with a gold crown. The shield is crowned with a Kazan cap. According to the traditions of heraldry, the dragon symbolizes power, wisdom and invincibility, the earth—life and wealth, the crown-development, and the cap above the shield-the capital of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_and_municipal_status">Administrative and municipal status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Administrative and municipal status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Kazan is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> of the republic.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Within the <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Russia#Administrative_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Subdivisions of Russia">framework of administrative divisions</a>, it is incorporated as the <b><a href="/wiki/City_of_federal_subject_significance" title="City of federal subject significance">city of republic significance</a> of Kazan</b>—an administrative unit with the status equal to that of the <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_Republic_of_Tatarstan" title="Administrative divisions of the Republic of Tatarstan">districts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref1500_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref1500-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> As a <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Russia#Municipal_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Subdivisions of Russia">municipal division</a>, the city of republic significance of Kazan is incorporated as <b>Kazan Urban Okrug</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref894_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref894-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_divisions">City divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: City divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D1%85%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/%D0%A1%D1%85%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8.jpg/220px-%D0%A1%D1%85%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/%D0%A1%D1%85%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8.jpg/330px-%D0%A1%D1%85%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/%D0%A1%D1%85%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8.jpg/440px-%D0%A1%D1%85%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8.jpg 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="497" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D1%85%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>City districts of Kazan</div></div></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Kazan" title="Economy of Kazan">Economy of Kazan</a></div>

built by <a href="/wiki/Kazan_Helicopters" title="Kazan Helicopters">Kazan Helicopters</a></div></div></div></div>
<p>Kazan is one of the largest industrial and financial centers of Russia, and a leading city of the <a href="/wiki/Volga_economic_region" title="Volga economic region">Volga economic region</a> in construction and accumulated investment.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The city's <a href="/wiki/Gross_Regional_Product" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross Regional Product">gross regional product</a> was 380 billion rubles in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Total banking capital of Kazan banks is third in Russia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The main industries of the city are: mechanical engineering, chemical, petrochemical, light and food industries. An innovative economy is represented by the largest IT-park in Russia which is one of the largest of its kind among Eastern European <a href="/wiki/Science_park" title="Science park">science parks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Kazan ranks 174th (highest in Russia) in <a href="/wiki/Mercer_(consulting_firm)" title="Mercer (consulting firm)">Mercer</a>’s Worldwide Quality of Living Survey.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Investments">Investments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Investments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2011, city organisations and businesses attracted more than 87 billion rubles for economy and social sphere development. This was 44% more than in 2010. In 2014, businesses attracted 86 billion rubles. Most of them have been implemented in the real economy sector.
</p><p>Because of the unstable economic situation within the country, there was a decrease of investment rates in 2015 and—according to the statistics of the first part of the year—it composed 51684.2 million rubles.
</p><p>There are head offices of six companies that are in the top 500 in terms of revenues in Russia. The total area of city business centres is 330 thousand square metres.
</p><p>Innovative economy in Kazan is represented by the biggest IT-park in Russia and also the biggest technical park in Europe. The only online platform for governmental trade except the Moscow one is operated in Kazan. During the post-Soviet period Kazan was the leader in terms of house construction in the Volga region, and now it holds the position and implements the Republican program of liquidation of dilapidated housing which was unique for Russia.
</p><p>According to <i>Forbes</i>, Kazan was ranked 15th among the "Best cities for business in Russia" of 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, Kazan ranked 6th in the quality of city environment rating, which was made by the Russian Federation Ministry of Regional Development, Russian Alliance of Engineers, Federal Construction Agency, Federal Service of Supervision of Consumer Protection and Welfare and Moscow Federal University.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%B5%D1%84%D0%B0%D0%B72850.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/%D0%9D%D0%B5%D1%84%D0%B0%D0%B72850.jpg/220px-%D0%9D%D0%B5%D1%84%D0%B0%D0%B72850.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/%D0%9D%D0%B5%D1%84%D0%B0%D0%B72850.jpg/330px-%D0%9D%D0%B5%D1%84%D0%B0%D0%B72850.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/%D0%9D%D0%B5%D1%84%D0%B0%D0%B72850.jpg/440px-%D0%9D%D0%B5%D1%84%D0%B0%D0%B72850.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%B5%D1%84%D0%B0%D0%B72850.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Neftekamsk_Automotive_Plant" title="Neftekamsk Automotive Plant">NefAZ</a> bus on Tukay Square</div></div></div>
<p>The first bus routes in Kazan came to use in 1925.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The bus is the most popular type of public transport in Kazan: in 2016, it carried about 74% of passengers. As of 2017, there are about 62 bus routes in the city,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> with a total length of more than 1.2 thousand km. The total number of buses operating on city routes is 840. The movement of all buses is monitored using an automated control system based on satellite navigation.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Any Internet user can track the movement of buses.
</p><p>Kazan's bus system was totally renovated in 2007. 62 routes have an aggregate length of 1,981 km (1,231 mi). All 1,444 buses are colored red. Half of the buses are imported, produced by <a href="/wiki/Golden_Dragon_(company)" title="Golden Dragon (company)">Golden Dragon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Higer_Bus" title="Higer Bus">Higer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minsk_Automobile_Plant" title="Minsk Automobile Plant">MAZ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yutong" title="Yutong">Yutong</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Motor_Company" title="Hyundai Motor Company">Hyundai</a>. Other buses are mostly Russian made <a href="/wiki/Neftekamsk_Automotive_Plant" title="Neftekamsk Automotive Plant">NefAZ</a>.
</p><p>The fare is 30 rubles in cash, 27 rubles by electronic card (2020). On the routes, conductors are involved and, in addition to paying for cash (with a higher fare), there are general civil (with different tariff plans for replenishment, including time passes and an "electronic wallet"), as well as preferential electronic transport cards.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tram">Tram</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tram">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazan_tram_on_Kirovskaya_Dike_08-2016_img1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Kazan_tram_on_Kirovskaya_Dike_08-2016_img1.jpg/220px-Kazan_tram_on_Kirovskaya_Dike_08-2016_img1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Kazan_tram_on_Kirovskaya_Dike_08-2016_img1.jpg/330px-Kazan_tram_on_Kirovskaya_Dike_08-2016_img1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Kazan_tram_on_Kirovskaya_Dike_08-2016_img1.jpg/440px-Kazan_tram_on_Kirovskaya_Dike_08-2016_img1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3496" data-file-height="2622" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazan_tram_on_Kirovskaya_Dike_08-2016_img1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An AKSM-843 tram passing by the Kirovskaya Dike</div></div></div>
<p>Kazan's tram system is one of the oldest tram systems in Russia, opened on 20 November 1899. The tram system in Kazan consists of five operating routes. The daily output is 82 trams. Most of the tram lines are laid along the axis of the main streets, most of them on a dedicated track, fenced with side stones. The tram in the city center was largely removed in the 2000s due to the fight against traffic jams on narrow streets; some routes turned out to be unprofitable after the optimization of the transport scheme in 2006–2007.
</p><p>In 2009–2020, the reconstruction of tram tracks on the main highways was carried out, as well as the construction of four new tram lines, which made it possible to launch circular tram routes No. 5/5a with an accelerated mode of movement in 2012-2020 along the sections of the Big Kazan Ring.
</p><p>All trams are equipped with autoinformators, announcements in which are in three languages (Russian, Tatar, English), for this reason announcements are played for a very long time (up to one and a half minutes). The fare is 30 rubles in cash, 27 rubles for an electronic card (2020). On the routes, conductors are involved and, in addition to paying for cash (with a higher fare), there are general civil (with different tariff plans for replenishment, including time passes and an "electronic wallet"), as well as preferential electronic transport cards.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trolleybus">Trolleybus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Trolleybus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:411%3D2019.08.25%3D%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%B9%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%81%3D5-%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88%D1%80%D1%83%D1%82(%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C)%3DDSC_0277.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/411%3D2019.08.25%3D%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%B9%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%81%3D5-%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88%D1%80%D1%83%D1%82%28%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C%29%3DDSC_0277.JPG/220px-411%3D2019.08.25%3D%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%B9%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%81%3D5-%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88%D1%80%D1%83%D1%82%28%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C%29%3DDSC_0277.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/411%3D2019.08.25%3D%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%B9%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%81%3D5-%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88%D1%80%D1%83%D1%82%28%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C%29%3DDSC_0277.JPG/330px-411%3D2019.08.25%3D%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%B9%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%81%3D5-%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88%D1%80%D1%83%D1%82%28%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C%29%3DDSC_0277.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/411%3D2019.08.25%3D%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%B9%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%81%3D5-%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88%D1%80%D1%83%D1%82%28%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C%29%3DDSC_0277.JPG/440px-411%3D2019.08.25%3D%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%B9%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%81%3D5-%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88%D1%80%D1%83%D1%82%28%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C%29%3DDSC_0277.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:411%3D2019.08.25%3D%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%B9%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%81%3D5-%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88%D1%80%D1%83%D1%82(%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C)%3DDSC_0277.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">Trolleybus</a> passing by the overpass on Richard Sorge Street</div></div></div>
<p>Kazan's trolleybus system is one of the oldest in Russia. Operation opened on 27 November 1948. In recent years, it continues to develop: new lines were launched, built and planned, while some new trolleybus lines replaced the removed tram lines. Two trolleybus depots operate a fleet of over 200 trolleybuses, all of which are green,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> and serve 10 routes with a total length of 359.9&#160;km (223.63&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> At the beginning of the XXI century, at the Kazan aircraft plant KAPO for the city, a major overhaul (CWR) of old trolleybuses was carried out.
</p><p>The fare is 30 rubles in cash, 27 rubles by electronic card (2020). On the routes, conductors are involved and, in addition to paying for cash (with a higher fare), there are general civil (with different tariff plans for replenishment, including time passes and an "electronic wallet"), as well as preferential electronic transport cards.
</p><p>All trolleybuses are monitored by an automated control system based on satellite navigation. Any Internet user can track the movement of trolleybuses.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metro">Metro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Metro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A single-line <a href="/wiki/Kazan_Metro" title="Kazan Metro">Kazan Metro</a> (running north to south-east), opened on 27 August 2005, the first and only metro system built in a post-soviet state after the collapse of the USSR. As of 2020, the Kazan Metro now has eleven stations, and crosses the <a href="/wiki/Kazanka_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazanka River">Kazanka River</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railways">Railways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Railways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazan_Railway_station_08-2016_img1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Kazan_Railway_station_08-2016_img1.jpg/220px-Kazan_Railway_station_08-2016_img1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Kazan_Railway_station_08-2016_img1.jpg/330px-Kazan_Railway_station_08-2016_img1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Kazan_Railway_station_08-2016_img1.jpg/440px-Kazan_Railway_station_08-2016_img1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4990" data-file-height="2495" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazan_Railway_station_08-2016_img1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kazan_railway_station" title="Kazan railway station">Kazan–Passazhirskaya</a>, opened in 1894</div></div></div>
<p>Kazan is connected with <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ulyanovsk" title="Ulyanovsk">Ulyanovsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yoshkar-Ola" title="Yoshkar-Ola">Yoshkar-Ola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yekaterinburg" title="Yekaterinburg">Yekaterinburg</a> by train.
</p><p>The main railway station <a href="/wiki/Kazan_railway_station" title="Kazan railway station">Kazan–Passazhirskaya</a> is located in the city centre and includes a main building (built in 1896), a commuter trains terminal, a ticket office building and some other technical buildings. The station serves 36 intercity trains,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> and more than eight million passengers per annum. The second terminus called "Kazan-2" is situated in the northern part of the city. Kazan also has 19 platforms for commuter trains.
</p><p>In addition, within the city there are also 24 railway stations and stopping platforms
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transit">Public transit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Public transit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Payment is received in cash, by dedicated travel cards and by banking cards. One ride fee is 27 rubles in cash or by banking card and 25 rubles by travel card.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> There are various plans for different types of travel which reduce single ride fees. There are no zoning tariffs within the city.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cycling">Cycling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Cycling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 1 July 2013, the Veli'k bicycle sharing system was launched in Kazan. In total, the system includes seven self-service bicycle docking stations, and a total fleet of 100 bikes. The service is open to anyone from 16 years of age. There are three types of subscription - monthly, weekly and daily. During the season from late spring to mid-autumn, residents and guests of Kazan typically use the service more than 15,000 times.
</p><p>In 2015, the first cycle routes on separate bike lanes were opened in the city centre; further expansion is planned throughout the city.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Waterways">Waterways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Waterways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rachport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Rachport.jpg/220px-Rachport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Rachport.jpg/330px-Rachport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Rachport.jpg/440px-Rachport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1520" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rachport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kazanskiy Rechnoy Port</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazan_Bulak_near_Kremlin_08-2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Kazan_Bulak_near_Kremlin_08-2016.jpg/220px-Kazan_Bulak_near_Kremlin_08-2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Kazan_Bulak_near_Kremlin_08-2016.jpg/330px-Kazan_Bulak_near_Kremlin_08-2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Kazan_Bulak_near_Kremlin_08-2016.jpg/440px-Kazan_Bulak_near_Kremlin_08-2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4098" data-file-height="2562" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazan_Bulak_near_Kremlin_08-2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Bolaq" title="Bolaq">Bolaq Canal</a></div></div></div>
<p>Kazan's river port is one of the largest on the <a href="/wiki/Volga" title="Volga">Volga</a>, thanks to the system of canals from which Kazan is sometimes called the "port of five seas".
</p><p>The main building of the river station was built together with the new river port by the early 1960s and renovated in 2005. The station serves both passengers of intercity cruise ships and commuter boats (including high-speed fleet) - to the Kamsky Ustye, Tetyush, Bolgar, Pechishch, Sviyazhsk and Sadovaya. The daily passenger traffic in the summer period is up to 6 thousand people per day. In winter, <a href="/wiki/Hovercraft" title="Hovercraft">Pneumocushion boats</a> are used, it goes from Kazan to Verkhny Uslon.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Highways">Highways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Highways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are federal highway connections to <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ufa" title="Ufa">Ufa</a> (<a href="/wiki/European_route_E22" title="European route E22">E-22</a>), <a href="/wiki/Orenburg" title="Orenburg">Orenburg</a> (R-239), <a href="/wiki/Ul%27yanovsk" class="mw-redirect" title="Ul&#39;yanovsk">Ul'yanovsk</a> (R-241) and Igra (R-242). There are also the R-175 federal highway and "Northern Europe – Western China" (in construction) route near the city.
</p><p>There are five bridges across the Kazanka (Qazansu) river in the city, and one bridge connecting Kazan with the opposite bank of the Volga.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Intercity_buses">Intercity buses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Intercity buses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are two bus stations in Kazan—Central and Southern. Bus routes connect Kazan with all districts of Tatarstan, <a href="/wiki/Samara,_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Samara, Russia">Samara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ufa" title="Ufa">Ufa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tolyatti" title="Tolyatti">Tolyatti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orenburg" title="Orenburg">Orenburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ulyanovsk" title="Ulyanovsk">Ulyanovsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheboksary" title="Cheboksary">Cheboksary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sterlitamak" title="Sterlitamak">Sterlitamak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buzuluk,_Orenburg_Oblast" title="Buzuluk, Orenburg Oblast">Buzuluk</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Baki,_Sukoharjo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Baki, Sukoharjo (page does not exist)">Baki</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aktobe" title="Aktobe">Aktobe</a>. It is planned to build new stations in the East, West and North districts instead of Central for relieving city centre.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kazan_International_Airport">Kazan International Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Kazan International Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%B0%D1%8D%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%B0%D1%8D%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C.JPG/330px-%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%B0%D1%8D%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%B0%D1%8D%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C.JPG/440px-%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%B0%D1%8D%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="3216" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%B0%D1%8D%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kazan International Airport</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kazan_International_Airport" title="Kazan International Airport">Kazan International Airport</a> is located 26 kilometers (16&#160;mi) from the city center. It is a hub for <a href="/wiki/UVT_Aero" title="UVT Aero">UVT Aero</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kazan_Air_Enterprise" title="Kazan Air Enterprise">Kazan Air Enterprise</a> and hosts eleven air companies. The airport is connected with the city by bus route #97 and by a suburban train line.
</p><p>There is also the <a href="/wiki/Kazan_Borisoglebskoye" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazan Borisoglebskoye">Kazan Borisoglebskoye</a> airfield, home to <a href="/wiki/Kazan_Aircraft_Production_Association" title="Kazan Aircraft Production Association">Kazan Aircraft Production Association</a>, a major aircraft factory, famous in the past as "Aircraft Plant 22" ("22nd Zavod").
</p><p>Adjacent to it lies a huge aircraft engines plant ("16th Zavod"). It produces versions of <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-204" title="Tupolev Tu-204">Tupolev 204</a> and 214 aircraft. In the past an Ilyushin-62, four-engine Russian mainliner, <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-160" title="Tupolev Tu-160">Tupolev-160 "Black Jack"</a> supersonic strategic bomber and <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-22M" title="Tupolev Tu-22M">Tu-22M tactic bomber</a> were also produced here. Both these plants and adjacent workers' housing make a whole city district known as "Aviastroitelny" ("Aircraft Builders").
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazan_population.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Kazan_population.gif/220px-Kazan_population.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Kazan_population.gif/330px-Kazan_population.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Kazan_population.gif/440px-Kazan_population.gif 2x" data-file-width="936" data-file-height="538" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazan_population.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population of Kazan since 1800</div></div></div>
<p>Population: <span class="nowrap">1,143,535&#8201;(<a href="/wiki/Russian_Census_(2010)" title="Russian Census (2010)">2010 Census</a>)</span>;<sup id="cite_ref-2010Census_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010Census-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> <span class="nowrap">1,105,289&#8201;(<a href="/wiki/Russian_Census_(2002)" title="Russian Census (2002)">2002 Census</a>)</span>;<sup id="cite_ref-PopCensus_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopCensus-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> <span class="nowrap">1,094,378&#8201;(<a href="/wiki/Soviet_Census_(1989)" title="Soviet Census (1989)">1989 Census</a>)</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Census1989_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census1989-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Kazan_metropolitan_area" title="Kazan metropolitan area">Kazan metropolitan area</a>'s population is 1.65 million.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity">Ethnicity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Ethnicity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kazan_ethnic_communities" title="Kazan ethnic communities">Kazan ethnic communities</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Young_Women_in_the_Street_-_Kazan_-_Russia.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Young_Women_in_the_Street_-_Kazan_-_Russia.JPG/220px-Young_Women_in_the_Street_-_Kazan_-_Russia.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Young_Women_in_the_Street_-_Kazan_-_Russia.JPG/330px-Young_Women_in_the_Street_-_Kazan_-_Russia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Young_Women_in_the_Street_-_Kazan_-_Russia.JPG/440px-Young_Women_in_the_Street_-_Kazan_-_Russia.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Young_Women_in_the_Street_-_Kazan_-_Russia.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Young women in the street, outside <a href="/wiki/Kazan_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazan University">Kazan University</a></div></div></div>
<p>The city's population consists mostly of ethnic <a href="/wiki/Volga_Tatars" title="Volga Tatars">Tatars</a> (47.6%) and ethnic <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> (48.6%). The other ethnicities are <a href="/wiki/Chuvash_people" title="Chuvash people">Chuvash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijani people">Azerbaijanis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_people" title="Vietnamese people">Vietnamese</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Jew" class="mw-redirect" title="Jew">Jews</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Interfaith_relations_in_Kazan,_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Interfaith relations in Kazan, Russia">Interfaith relations in Kazan, Russia</a></div>
<p>Predominant faiths of Kazan city are <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Islam</a> and Eastern <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christianity" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Christianity">Orthodox Christianity</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> with minority representation of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholicism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Its common to find the <a href="/wiki/Tatar_language" title="Tatar language">Tatar language</a> being spoken in the city, mainly by Tatars.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Kazan has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a>: <i>Dfb</i>) with long, cold winters (colder than <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>), and warm, sunny summers. As a result of its far inland position, summers are extremely warm for its latitude and winters are quite cold compared to areas further west in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The warmest month is July with daily mean temperature near 20.2&#160;°C (68.4&#160;°F), and the coldest month is January, with a daily mean of −10.4&#160;°C (13.3&#160;°F).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The city set its two hottest days on record during the <a href="/wiki/2010_Northern_Hemisphere_summer_heat_waves" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 Northern Hemisphere summer heat waves">2010 Northern Hemisphere summer heat waves</a>. Temperatures reached +39&#160;°C (102&#160;°F) in the hottest days during that time.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_Kazan">Central Kazan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Central Kazan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazan_Kremlin_Qolsharif_Mosque_08-2016_img2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Kazan_Kremlin_Qolsharif_Mosque_08-2016_img2.jpg/170px-Kazan_Kremlin_Qolsharif_Mosque_08-2016_img2.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Kazan_Kremlin_Qolsharif_Mosque_08-2016_img2.jpg/255px-Kazan_Kremlin_Qolsharif_Mosque_08-2016_img2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Kazan_Kremlin_Qolsharif_Mosque_08-2016_img2.jpg/340px-Kazan_Kremlin_Qolsharif_Mosque_08-2016_img2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2605" data-file-height="3473" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazan_Kremlin_Qolsharif_Mosque_08-2016_img2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Qol%C5%9F%C3%A4rif_Mosque" class="mw-redirect" title="Qolşärif Mosque">Qolşärif Mosque</a> grand mosque</div></div></div>
