<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kremlin">Kremlin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Kremlin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kazan_Kremlin" title="Kazan Kremlin">Kazan Kremlin</a></div>
<table class="box-Unreferenced plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Kazan%22">"Kazan"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Kazan%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Kazan%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Kazan%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Kazan%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Kazan%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2018</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The city has a citadel (Russian: кремль, tr. kreml', or sometimes Tatar: <i>kirman</i>), which was declared a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> in 2000. Major monuments in the Kremlin are the five-domed, six-columned Annunciation Cathedral (1561–62) and the mysterious, formerly leaning <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6yembik%C3%A4_Tower" title="Söyembikä Tower">Söyembikä Tower</a>, named after the last queen of Kazan and regarded as the city's most conspicuous landmark.
</p><p>Also of interest are the towers and walls, erected in the 16th and 17th centuries but later reconstructed; the <a href="/wiki/Qolsharif_mosque" class="mw-redirect" title="Qolsharif mosque">Qol-Şarif Mosque</a>, which has been rebuilt inside the citadel; remains of the Saviour Monastery (a 16th-century cathedral demolished by the Bolsheviks) with the Spasskaya Tower; and the Governor's House (1843–53), designed by <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Thon" title="Konstantin Thon">Konstantin Thon</a>, now the Palace of the <a href="/wiki/President_(government_title)" title="President (government title)">President</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tatarstan" title="Tatarstan">Tatarstan</a>.
</p><p>Next door, the ornate baroque Sts-Peter-and-Paul's Cathedral on Qawi Nacmi Street and Marcani Mosque on Qayum Nasiri Street date back to the 18th century.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Towers">Towers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Towers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Spasskaya Tower was built in two floors by 16th century Pskov architects Ivan Shiryai and Postnik Yakovlev. From the inside, the northern side of the fortress to the Spasskaya Tower adjoined the gate to Spasskaya Church, which has now merged with the tower. The typical Pskovian architectural elements of the facade face the main street of the Kremlin. At the end of the 17th century, instead of three tiers, the tower was built with two brick eight-sided tiers with a brick roof, getting its present, familiar appearance. Until 1917, the tower was crowned with the double-headed coat of arms of the Russian state. In the 18th century, a ringing clock was installed in the upper tier, and even earlier a large bell was moved from a small belfry (now lost, located on the castle wall on the left side of the tower). Until the middle of the 19th century, there was a moat with a stone bridge in front of the tower.
</p><p>The South-Western Tower was built simultaneously with the Spasskaya tower by Pskov masters and is a classic example of the Pskov style of defensive structures.
</p><p>The name of the Transfiguration Tower comes from the Transfiguration Monastery of the Savior, which was fenced from the north-west. The tower was also built by Pskov architects Postnik and Barma, but it was significantly rebuilt later, as it has strong traces of the architectural influence of the Moscow defensive architecture. The territory from the Transfiguration Tower to the Spasskaya pass was added to the old Khan's fortress by Pskov masters.
</p><p>There are unnamed round brick towers, presumably built by Moscow architects in the 17th century.
</p><p>The Tainitskaya Tower was built in its present form in the 1550s by Postnik Yakovlev. It was named after a secret source from which it was possible to take water during a siege. The entrance to the tower is in the form of a "knee", which increased the defense of the Kremlin. It replaced a tower from the time of the khanate, Nur Ali (in Russian transcription Muraleeva). The 22-year-old Tsar Ivan the Terrible entered the conquered city through the Nur Ali tower.
</p><p>The North-Eastern Round Tower was demolished after the Pugachev's assault.
</p><p>The Consistor Tower was built in brick by Moscow architects in the 17th century, its name was given in the 18th century from the Spiritual Consistory located near the tower in the Kremlin. Near the tower, archaeological excavations revealed the so-called Tezitsky (Arabic for "merchant") Moat, which went from the Consistor Tower to the Transfiguration. Archaeologist N. Kalinin and a number of scientists believed that the moat was the southern border of the Khan's fortress.
</p><p>The Southeast Round Tower is an example of Pskov architecture of the 16th century.
</p>
<h3><span id="Bist.C3.A4.2C_or_Posad"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bistä,_or_Posad">Bistä, or Posad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Bistä, or Posad">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Central Kazan is divided into two districts by the <a href="/wiki/Bolaq" title="Bolaq">Bolaq</a> canal and Lake <a href="/wiki/Qaban_lakes" class="mw-redirect" title="Qaban lakes">Qaban</a>. The first district (Qazan Bistäse or Kazanskiy Posad), historically Russian, is situated on the hill, the second (İske Tatar Bistäse or Staro-Tatarskaya Sloboda), historically Tatar, is situated between the Bolaq and the Volga. Mosques, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Nurullah_Mosque" class="mw-redirect" title="Nurullah Mosque">Nurullah</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Soltan" class="mw-redirect" title="Soltan">Soltan</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Bornay_Mosque" title="Bornay Mosque">Bornay</a></i>, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Apanay&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Apanay (page does not exist)">Apanay</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/%C3%84cem" class="mw-redirect" title="Äcem">Äcem</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Marcani_Mosque" class="mw-redirect" title="Marcani Mosque">Märcani</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/%C4%B0ske_Ta%C5%9F" class="mw-redirect" title="İske Taş">İske Taş</a></i>, <i>Zäñgär</i> are in the Tatar district. Churches, such as <i>Blagoveschenskaya</i>, <i>Varvarinskaya</i>, <i>Nikol'skaya</i>, <i>Tikhvinskaya</i>, are mostly in the Russian part of the city. The main city-centre streets are <i><a href="/wiki/Baumana_Street,_Kazan" class="mw-redirect" title="Baumana Street, Kazan">Bauman</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Kremlyovskaya_Street" title="Kremlyovskaya Street">Kremlyovskaya</a></i>, <i>Dzerzhinsky</i>, <i>Tuqay</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pushkin_Street,_Kazan" title="Pushkin Street, Kazan">Puşkin</a></i>, <i>Butlerov</i>, <i>Gorkiy</i>, <i>Karl Marx</i> and <i>Märcani</i>.
</p><p>An old legend says that in 1552, before the Russian invasion, wealthy Tatars (<i>baylar</i>) hid gold and silver in Lake Qaban.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wooden_Kazan">Wooden Kazan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Wooden Kazan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the beginning of the 1900s most of Central Kazan was covered by wooden buildings, usually consisting of two floors. There was a historical environment of Kazan citizens, but not the best place to live in. During the Republican program "The liquidation of ramshackle apartments" most of them (unlike other Russian cities), especially in Central Kazan, where the land is not cheap, were destroyed and their population was moved to new areas at the suburb of the city (Azino, Azino-2, Quartal 39). Nearly 100,000 citizens resettled by this programme.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_major_buildings">Other major buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Other major buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Another significant building in central Kazan is the former "Smolentzev and Shmelev" tea house and hotel, now the Shalyapin Palace Hotel. It is located at 7/80 Universitetskaya Street, at the corner of Universitetskaya and Bauman. A major landmark of late-19th and early-20th century commercial architecture, it consists of two portions. The original portion, built for a merchant named Usmanov in the 1860s, was bought by the inter-related families of Efim Smolentzev and Pavel and Nikolai Shmelev in 1899.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> They operated a store selling, among other things, tea. In 1910, the Smolentevs and Shmelevs constructed another portion, designed by architect Vasili Trifonov, and operated a hotel there.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> After the Russian Revolution, the building eventually became the Hotel Soviet and after 2000 it was heavily renovated to reopen as the Shalyapin Palace Hotel.
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 235px"><div style="width: 235px">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:100%;max-width:890px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazan_cityscape.jpg" class="image" title="A panoramic view of Kazan Kremlin, Vernicle temple and Kazanka river right bank"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Kazan_cityscape.jpg/882px-Kazan_cityscape.jpg" decoding="async" width="882" height="140" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Kazan_cityscape.jpg/1323px-Kazan_cityscape.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/eb/Kazan_cityscape.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="238" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazan_cityscape.jpg" title="File:Kazan cityscape.jpg"> </a></div>A panoramic view of Kazan Kremlin, Vernicle temple and Kazanka river right bank</div></div></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_science">Education and science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Education and science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_education">Primary and secondary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Primary and secondary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Primary and secondary education system of Kazan includes:
</p>
<ul><li>282 nurseries, most of which are municipal</li>
<li>178 schools, 2 of which are private</li>
<li>28 vocational technical schools</li>
<li>15 colleges</li>
<li>10 special colleges</li></ul>
<p>There are also 49 music schools, 43 sports school, and 10 fine-arts schools, including the <a href="/wiki/Kazan_Art_School" title="Kazan Art School">Kazan Art School</a> founded in 1895.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">Higher education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Higher education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Kazan_Universities" title="List of Kazan Universities">List of Kazan Universities</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazan_state_university.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Kazan_state_university.jpg/220px-Kazan_state_university.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Kazan_state_university.jpg/330px-Kazan_state_university.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Kazan_state_university.jpg/440px-Kazan_state_university.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="435" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kazan_state_university.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kazan_(Volga_region)_Federal_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazan (Volga region) Federal University">Kazan Federal University</a></div></div></div>
<p>There are 44 institutes of higher education in Kazan, including 19 branches of universities from other cities. More than 140,000 students are educated in the city.
<a href="/wiki/Kazan_Federal_University" title="Kazan Federal University">Kazan Federal University</a> (founded in 1804) is third oldest university in <a href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Federation">Russia</a> after <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_State_University" title="Saint Petersburg State University">Saint Petersburg State University</a> (1724) and <a href="/wiki/Lomonosov_Moscow_State_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Lomonosov Moscow State University">Moscow State University</a> (1755). In 2009 KFU got Federal status as main university of <a href="/wiki/Volga_Federal_District" title="Volga Federal District">Volga Region</a>.
Some other prominent universities are:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Kazan_State_Technical_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazan State Technical University">Kazan State Technical University</a> – founded in 1932. In 2009 it got status of National university</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kazan_State_Medical_University" title="Kazan State Medical University">Kazan State Medical University</a> – founded in 1814 as a department within <a href="/wiki/Kazan_State_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazan State University">Kazan State University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kazan_State_Technological_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazan State Technological University">Kazan State Technological University</a> – founded in 1919 on the base of pre-existing vocational school</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kazan_Conservatory" title="Kazan Conservatory">Kazan State Conservatory</a> – founded in 1945</li>
<li>Volga Region State Academy of Physical Culture, Sport and Tourism<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> founded in July 2010 in the framework of the XXVII World Summer Universiade Legacy. The branch, located in Naberezhnye Chelny, will proceed functioning.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science">Science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tatarstan_Acad_Sci.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Tatarstan_Acad_Sci.jpg/220px-Tatarstan_Acad_Sci.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Tatarstan_Acad_Sci.jpg/330px-Tatarstan_Acad_Sci.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Tatarstan_Acad_Sci.jpg/440px-Tatarstan_Acad_Sci.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="409" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tatarstan_Acad_Sci.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Main building of Tatarstan Academy of Sciences</div></div></div>
<p>Kazan is a major scientific centre in Russia. Kazan formed a big number of scientific areas and schools (mathematical, chemical, medical, linguistic, geological, geobotanical, etc.). Scientific discoveries are a subject of special pride, including: the creation of non-Euclidean geometry (<a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Lobachevsky" title="Nikolai Lobachevsky">Nikolai Lobachevsky</a>), the discovery of the chemical element <a href="/wiki/Ruthenium" title="Ruthenium">ruthenium</a> (<a href="/wiki/Karl_Ernst_Claus" title="Karl Ernst Claus">Karl Ernst Claus</a>), the theory about the structure of organic compounds (<a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Butlerov" class="mw-redirect" title="Aleksandr Butlerov">Aleksandr Butlerov</a>), the discovery of the electron paramagnetic resonance (<a href="/wiki/Yevgeny_Zavoisky" title="Yevgeny Zavoisky">Yevgeny Zavoisky</a>) and acoustic paramagnetic resonance (Altshuler) and many others. The city hosts:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan_Science_Centre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kazan Science Centre (page does not exist)">Kazan Science Centre</a> of <a href="/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Russian Academy of Sciences">Russian Academy of Sciences</a>, since 1945. It includes 5 academic institutions.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tatarstan_Academy_of_Sciences&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tatarstan Academy of Sciences (page does not exist)">Tatarstan Academy of Sciences</a>, since 1991. It includes 7 local departments with 13 academic institutions (also, 21 organisations are under the guidance of TAS) and one branch in Ulyanovsk.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_health">Public health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Public health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The year 1814 is considered to be an official year of the beginning of scientific medicine in Kazan. Exactly at that time University Hospital was open. In 1930 Faculty of Medicine is separated from the Kazan Federal University and holds a lot of specialized hospitals under its patronage. Nowadays Kazan becomes the largest public health center in Russia. 120 medical organisations are operated in the city. Kazan Interregional clinical-diagnostic center is the largest in Volga region in cardiovascular and neurological diseases. The largest hospital in Kazan is Republican Clinical Hospital.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_administration">Government and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Government and administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mayor">Mayor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Mayor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Kazan_mayors" title="List of Kazan mayors">List of Kazan mayors</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_Duma">City Duma</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: City Duma">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan_City_Duma&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kazan City Duma (page does not exist)">Kazan City Duma</a> is a representative body of the city, elected every four years and holds its sessions in Kazan City Hall.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive_committee">Executive committee</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Executive committee">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Executive committee is a municipal body of the executive organs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The committee's head is Denis Kalinkin.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_of_the_Republic_of_Tatarstan">Government of the Republic of Tatarstan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Government of the Republic of Tatarstan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Kazan hosts Tatarstan President's residence and administration (in Kremlin), Tatarstan's Cabinet of Ministers and Council of State (on Freedom square).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Communication">Communication</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Communication">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Agency works 84 post offices belonging to the branch of "Russian Post", UFPS "Tatarstan pochtasy". The official opening of the Kazan city telephone network took place on 27 (15) November 1888. At the moment, there are four operators of wired telephone in Kazan. The total capacity of the telephone network in Kazan is about 456,000 numbers. Services of IP-telephony operators in addition to the basic wired connection is also supported by the five companies.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The city has six mobile operators (<a href="/wiki/Beeline_(brand)" title="Beeline (brand)">Beeline</a>, <a href="/wiki/MegaFon" title="MegaFon">MegaFon</a>, <a href="/wiki/MTS_(network_provider)" title="MTS (network provider)">MTS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tele2_Russia" title="Tele2 Russia">Tele2 Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Letai" class="mw-redirect" title="Letai">Letai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yota" title="Yota">Yota</a>, and also operates virtual mobile operator "Mobile public communication"). By the number of Internet users—428 thousand people—Kazan takes the 4th place in Russia. According to the General Director of <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google Russia</a> Vladimir Dolgov, Kazan is the largest center of information technology development, the level of Internet penetration is 75%, which is a record figure for Russia. Access to the World Wide Web in Kazan is provided by 15 operators.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The most popular forms of Internet access are cable networks and ADSL. Previously popular Dial-up has almost lost its position, at the same time actively developing wireless technology Wi-Fi and Wi-Max. Scartel launched the first <a href="/wiki/LTE_(telecommunication)" title="LTE (telecommunication)">LTE</a> network in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 30 August 2012 in Kazan, IT Park was held a launch ceremonyfor the fourth generation network (4G, LTE). LTE network in Kazan was launched by three operators - Scartel LLC (Yota trademark), MegaFon OJSC and MTS OJSC. On 27 June 2014, the LTE network of mobile operator Fly was launched.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>Kazan now is one of the most developed cities in Russia in terms of sport. The city has hosted two <a href="/wiki/Bandy_World_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="Bandy World Championships">Bandy World Championships</a>, in 2005 and 2011, the World Summer Universiade 2013, the World Championship in fencing in 2014, the Aquatics Championship FINA 2015, 2017 FIFA Confederations Cup, 2018 FIFA World Cup and other international competitions of various levels. In the future the city will hold the 2022 Special Olympics World Winter Games.
</p><p>The city of Kazan is a leader in terms of winnings in various sports including its most popular sports teams.
</p><p>Men's teams:

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Kazan_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazan Arena">Kazan Arena</a> – stadium with capacity 45,000, home ground for <a href="/wiki/FC_Rubin_Kazan" title="FC Rubin Kazan">FC Rubin</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Central_Stadium_(Kazan)" title="Central Stadium (Kazan)">Central stadium</a> – Olympic stadium, capacity 30,133. Ex-home ground for FC Rubin.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TatNeft_Arena" title="TatNeft Arena">TatNeft Arena</a> – indoor sporting arena, capacity 10,000. Home to <a href="/wiki/Aq_Bars_Kazan" class="mw-redirect" title="Aq Bars Kazan">HSC Aq Bars</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Basket-Hall_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Basket-Hall Arena">Basket-Hall</a> – indoor sporting arena, capacity 7,000 (large hall) and 1,500 (small hall). Home to <a href="/wiki/UNICS_Kazan" class="mw-redirect" title="UNICS Kazan">BC UNICS</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kazan_Volleyball_Centre" title="Kazan Volleyball Centre">Kazan Volleyball Centre</a>, capacity 4,600. Home to <a href="/wiki/VC_Zenit_Kazan" class="mw-redirect" title="VC Zenit Kazan">VC Zenit</a> and WVC Dynamo-Kazan.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Raketa_Stadium" title="Raketa Stadium">Raketa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trudovye_Rezervy_Stadium_(Kazan)" title="Trudovye Rezervy Stadium (Kazan)">Trudovye Rezervy</a> ice stadiums</li></ul>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/2022_Special_Olympics_World_Winter_Games" title="2022 Special Olympics World Winter Games">2022 Special Olympics World Winter Games</a></li>
<li>2019 Candidates Tournament for the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_World_Chess_Championship_2019" class="mw-redirect" title="Women&#39;s World Chess Championship 2019">Women's World Chess Championship 2019</a></li>
<li>2019 <a href="/wiki/WorldSkills" title="WorldSkills">WorldSkills</a> Championship</li>
<li>2018 <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a></li>
<li>2017 and 2018 Red Bull Air Race World Championship</li>
<li>Kazan is the host city for the <a href="/wiki/2013_Summer_Universiade" title="2013 Summer Universiade">2013 Summer Universiade</a>, <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Aquatics_Championships" title="2015 World Aquatics Championships">2015 World Aquatics Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/2017_FIFA_Confederations_Cup" title="2017 FIFA Confederations Cup">2017 FIFA Confederations Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>.</li>
<li>2016 – 28th International Olympiad in Informatics</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2016_European_Judo_Championships" title="2016 European Judo Championships">2016 European Judo Championships</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2014_European_Badminton_Championships" title="2014 European Badminton Championships">2014 European Badminton Championships</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2011_European_Weightlifting_Championships" title="2011 European Weightlifting Championships">2011 European Weightlifting Championships</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2005_Bandy_World_Championship" title="2005 Bandy World Championship">2005</a> and <a href="/wiki/2011_Bandy_World_Championship" title="2011 Bandy World Championship">2011 Bandy World Championship</a></li>
<li>2010 <a href="/wiki/Finswimming" title="Finswimming">finswimming</a> European championship</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Kazan is actively engaged in international activities. The city has foreign diplomatic, trade and cultural representations, the Kazan Kremlin and the Institute of culture of peace are under the auspices of <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>, the city participates in partner movements, is a member of the world organizations of cities. The summit of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a> heads, the Summit of the world security services and other important forums, conferences and events of the world level were held in Kazan. The head of <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, the us Secretary of state, about three dozen presidents and Prime Ministers of foreign States paid visits to the capital of the Republic, as to few other cities of the country. Renovated in 2005, the international airport provides flights to dozens of cities in different countries, including the largest Airliners (class Boeing 747), and is gradually being rebuilt into a potential hub for the Universiade 2013 and the World Cup 2018; international rail links from the city.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">Twin towns and sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Twin towns and sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Kazan" title="List of people from Kazan">List of people from Kazan</a></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Rashid_Nezhmetdinov" title="Rashid Nezhmetdinov">Rashid Nezhmetdinov</a>, International Master and five-time winner of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Chess_Championship" title="Russian Chess Championship">Russian Chess Championship</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dayana_Kirillova" title="Dayana Kirillova">Dayana Kirillova</a>, singer who represented <a href="/wiki/Russia_in_the_Junior_Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Russia in the Junior Eurovision Song Contest">Russia at the Junior Eurovision Song Contest</a> in <a href="/wiki/Junior_Eurovision_Song_Contest_2013" title="Junior Eurovision Song Contest 2013">2013</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sofya_Gulyak" title="Sofya Gulyak">Sofya Gulyak</a>, pianist, only female winner of the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_International_Piano_Competition" title="Leeds International Piano Competition">Leeds Piano Competition</a>, in 2009</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Venera_Gimadieva" title="Venera Gimadieva">Venera Gimadieva</a>, operatic soprano who has performed leading roles in major European opera houses</li></ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sources">Sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kazan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><span lang="ru" title="Russian-language text">Министерство юстиции Республики Татарстан.&#160;Приказ&#160;№01-02/9&#160;от&#160;4 февраля 2014 г. «Об утверждении реестра административно-территориальных единиц и населённых пунктов в Республике Татарстан», в ред. Приказа №01-02/160 от&#160;11 марта 2015 г.&#160;«О внесении изменений в Приказ Министерства юстиции Республики Татарстан от 04.02.2014 №01-02/9 "Об утверждении реестра административно-территориальных единиц и населённых пунктов в Республике Татарстан"».  Опубликован: Официальный сайт правовой информации Министерства юстиции Республики Татарстан (<a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://pravo.tatarstan.ru">http://pravo.tatarstan.ru</a>), 27 февраля 2014 г.</span> (Ministry of Justice of the Republic of Tatarstan.&#160;Order&#160;&#x23;01-02/9&#160;of&#160;February&#160;4, 2014 <i>On the Adoption of the Registry of the Administrative-Territorial Units and Inhabited Localities in the Republic of Tatarstan</i>, as amended by the Order&#160;&#x23;01-02/160 of&#160;March&#160;11, 2015 <i>On Amending the Order of the Ministry of Justice of the Republic of Tatarstan #01-02/9 of February&#160;4, 2014 "On the Adoption of the Registry of the Administrative-Territorial Units and Inhabited Localities in the Republic of Tatarstan"</i>. ).</li>
<li><span lang="ru" title="Russian-language text">Государственный Совет Республики Татарстан.&#160;Закон&#160;№46-ЗРТ&#160;от&#160;15 сентября 2004 г. «О границах территории и статусе муниципального образования города Казани», в ред. Закона №132-ЗРТ от&#160;26 декабря 2014 г.&#160;«Об изменении границ территорий отдельных муниципальных образований и внесении изменений в Законы Республики Татарстан "О границах территории и статусе муниципального образования города Казани" и "Об установлении границ территорий и статусе муниципального образования "Лаишевский муниципальный район" и муниципальных образований в его составе"». Вступил в силу&#160;со дня официального опубликования. Опубликован: "Республика Татарстан", №191, 21 сентября 2004 г.</span> (<a href="/wiki/State_Council_of_the_Republic_of_Tatarstan" title="State Council of the Republic of Tatarstan">State Council of the Republic of Tatarstan</a>.&#160;Law&#160;&#x23;46-ZRT&#160;of&#160;September&#160;15, 2004 <i>On the Borders of the Territory and the Status of the Municipal Formation of the City of Kazan</i>, as amended by the Law&#160;&#x23;132-ZRT of&#160;December&#160;26, 2014 <i>On Changing the Borders of the Territories of Various Municipal Formations and on Amending the Laws of the Republic of Tatarstan "On the Borders of the Territory and the Status of the Municipal Formation of the City of Kazan" and "On Establishing the Borders of the Territories and the Status of the Municipal Formation of "Laishevsky Municipal District" and of the Municipal Formations It Comprises"</i>. Effective as of&#160;the official publication date.).</li>
